394→\t\t\t}\n   395→\n   396→\t\t\tif delim == \"\" {\n   397→\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, env)\n   398→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   399→\t\t\t}\n   400→\n   401→\t\t\t// cut the string on the child key and error\n}\n\ntype deprecator interface {\n\tdeprecations(v *viper.Viper) []deprecated\n}\n\n// fieldKey returns the name to be used when deriving a fields env var key.\n// If marked as squash the key will be the empty string.\n// Otherwise, it is derived from the lowercase name of the field.\nfunc fieldKey(field reflect.StructField) string {\n\tif tag := field.Tag.Get(\"mapstructure\"); tag != \"\" {\n\t\ttag, attr, ok := strings.Cut(tag, \",\")\n\t\tif !ok || attr == \"squash\" || attr == \"omitempty\" {\n\t\t\treturn tag\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn strings.ToLower(field.Name)\n}\n\ntype envBinder interface {\n\tMustBindEnv(...string)\n}\n\n// bindEnvVars descends into the provided struct field binding any expected\n// environment variable keys it finds reflecting struct and field tags.\nfunc bindEnvVars(v envBinder, env, prefixes []string, typ reflect.Type) {\n\t// descend through pointers\n\tif typ.Kind() == reflect.Pointer {\n\t\ttyp = typ.Elem()\n\t}\n\n\tswitch typ.Kind() env, prefixes, structField.Type)\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tbind(env, prefixes, \"\", func(prefixes []string) {\n\t\tv.MustBindEnv(strings.Join(prefixes, \".\"))\n\t})\n}\n\nconst wildcard = \"*\"\n\nfunc appendIfNotEmpty(s []string, v ...string) []string {\n\tfor _, vs := range v {\n\t\tif vs != \"\" {\n\t\t\ts = append(s, vs)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// bind invokes the supplied function \"fn\" with each possible set of\n// prefixes for the next prefix (\"next\").\n// If the last prefix is \"*\" then we must search the current environment\n// for matching env vars to obtain the potential keys which populate\n// the unbound map keys.\nfunc bind(env, prefixes []string, next string, fn func([]string)) {\n\t// given the previous entry is non-existent or not the wildcard\n\tif len(prefixes) < 1 || prefixes[len(prefixes)-1] != wildcard {\n\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(prefixes, next))\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// drop the wildcard and derive all the possible keys from\n\t// existing environment variables.\n\tp := make([]string, len(prefixes)-1)\n\tcopy(p, prefixes[:len(prefixes)-1])\n\n\tvar (\n\t\t// makezero linter doesn't take note of subsequent copy\n\t\t// nolint https://github.com/ashanbrown/makezero/issues/12\n\t\tprefix = strings.ToUpper(strings.Join(append(p, \"\"), \"_\"))\n\t\tkeys   = strippedKeys(env, prefix, strings.ToUpper(next))\n\t)\n\n\tfor _, key := range keys {\n\t\tfn(appendIfNotEmpty(p, strings.ToLower(key), next))\n\t}\n}\n\n// strippedKeys returns a set of keys derived from a list of env var keys.\n// It starts by filtering and stripping each key with a matching prefix.\n// Given a child delimiter string is supplied it also trims the delimeter string\n// and any remaining characters after this suffix.\n//\n// e.g strippedKeys([\"A_B_C_D\", \"A_B_F_D\", \"A_B_E_D_G\"], \"A_B\", \"D\")\n// returns [\"c\", \"f\", \"e\"]\n//\n// It's purpose is to extract the parts of env vars which are likely\n// keys in an arbitrary map type.\nfunc strippedKeys(envs []string, prefix, delim string) (keys []string) {\n\tfor _, env := range envs {\n\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(env, prefix) {\n\t\t\tenv = env[len(prefix):]\n\t\t\tif env == \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif delim == \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, env)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// cut the string on the child key and take the left hand component\n\t\t\tif left, _, ok := strings.Cut(env, \"_\"+delim); ok {\n\t\t\t\tkeys = append(keys, left)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn\n}\n\n// getFliptEnvs returns all environment variables which have FLIPT_\n// as a prefix. It also strips this prefix before appending them to the\n// resulting set.\nfunc getFliptEnvs() (envs []string) {\n\tconst prefix = \"FLIPT_\"\n\tfor _, e := range os.Environ() {\n\t\tkey, _, ok := When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n   173→\n   174→Key areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n   175→\n   176→- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n   177→- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n   178→- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n   179→- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n   180→- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n   181→\n   182→#### Naming Conventions\n   183→\n   184→- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n   185→- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n   186→- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n   187→- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n   188→- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n   189→- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n   190→\n   191→#### Variable Declarations\n   192→\n   193→```go\n   194→// Prefer := for single variable declarations\n   195→result := SomeType{}\n   196→\n   197→// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\n   198→var (\n   199→    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n   200→    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n   201→    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n   202→)\n   203→```\n   204→\n   205→#### Constants\n   206→\n   207→Use constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n   208→\n   209→**❌ Bad Examples**\n   210→\n   211→```go\n   212→var (\n   213→    maxRetries = 3\n   214→    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n   215→)\n   216→```\n   217→\n   218→```go\n 285→    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n   286→)\n   287→```\n   288→\n   289→#### Logging\n   290→\n   291→Use structured logging with zap:\n   292→\n   293→```go\n   294→// Preferred - about what to log\n   307→```\n   308→\n   309→#### Comments and Documentation\n   310→\n   311→```go\n   312→// Public functions need godoc comments starting with function name\n   313→// ListFlags Playwright for E2E\n   410→\n   411→### Writing Effective Tests\n   412→\n   413→When writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n   414→\n   415→**❌ Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n   416→\n   417→```go\n   418→// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\n   419→func TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n   420→    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n   421→    require.NoError(t, err)\n   422→    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n   423→}\n   424→```\n   425→\n   426→**✅ Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n   427→\n   428→```go\n   429→// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\n   430→func TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n   431→    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n   432→    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   433→        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n   434→        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n   435→        return ok && value == expectedValue\n   436→    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n   437→    \n   438→    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n   439→    require.NoError(t, err)\n   440→    \n   441→    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n   442→    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n   443→    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n   444→}\n   445→```\n   446→\n   447→**Key Testing Principles:**\n   448→\n   449→- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n   450→- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n   451→- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n   452→- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n   453→- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n   454→\n   455→### Integration Tests\n   456→\n   457→Integration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. When in doubt, refer to the Google guide first, then apply these project-specific patterns.\n\nKey areas from the Google guide to pay special attention to:\n\n- **Formatting**: Use `gofmt` (we use `goimports` which includes `gofmt`)\n- **Naming**: Follow Go naming conventions for packages, types, functions, and variables\n- **Package organization**: Keep packages focused and avoid circular dependencies\n- **Error handling**: Return errors as the last return value, handle errors explicitly\n- **Documentation**: Write clear godoc comments for exported types and functions\n\n#### Naming Conventions\n\n- **Public functions**: Use PascalCase (`NewServer`, `ListFlags`, `RegisterGRPC`)\n- **Private functions**: Use camelCase (`getStore`, `buildConfig`, `handleError`)\n- **Factory functions**: Use `New` prefix for constructors (`NewRepository`, `NewEnvironmentFactory`)\n- **Variables**: Use camelCase (`environmentKey`, `namespaceKey`, `startTime`)\n- **Constants**: Use PascalCase for exported, camelCase for unexported\n- **Interfaces**: Use descriptive names (`Store`, `EnvironmentStore`, `Validator`)\n\n#### Variable Declarations\n\n```go\n// Prefer := for single variable declarations\nresult := SomeType{}\n\n// Use var blocks for multiple related variables\nvar (\n    environmentKey = r.EnvironmentKey\n    namespaceKey   = r.NamespaceKey\n    startTime      = time.Now().UTC()\n)\n```\n\n#### Constants\n\nUse constants when appropriate for values that are unlikely to change. Even in tests.\n\n**❌ Bad Examples**\n\n```go\nvar (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n```go\n  maxRetries := 3\n  secretProvider := \"vault\"\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example**\n\n```go\nconst (\n    maxRetries = 3\n    secretProvider = \"vault\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Error Handling\n\n##### Error Types\n\nUse the custom error types when possible:\n\n```go\n// Preferred - use custom error types\nreturn nil, errs.ErrNotFoundf(\"flag %q not found\", key)\nreturn nil, errs.ErrInvalidf(\"invalid configuration: %s\", reason)\n\n// Fallback - standard error handling\nreturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to process: %w\", err)\n```\n\n##### Inline Errors\n\nPrefer inline error declarations and checking when it makes sense.\n\n**❌ Bad Example**\n\n```go\nerr := doSomething()\nif err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example**\n\n```go\nif err := doSomething(); err != nil {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Imports\n\nFollow the three-group import pattern (extends Google guide):\n\n```go\nimport (\n    // Standard library\n    \"context\"\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"time\"\n\n    // Third-party packages\n    \"github.com/go-git/go-git/v6\"\n    \"go.uber.org/zap\"\n\n    // Local packages\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/errors\"\n    \"go.flipt.io/flipt/internal/config\"\n)\n```\n\n#### Logging\n\nUse structured logging with zap:\n\n```go\n// conditions\")\ns.logger.Error(\"error conditions that need attention\")\n\n// Avoid overusing log statements - be selective about what to log\n```\n\n#### Comments and Documentation\n\n```go\n// *flipt.ListFlagRequest) (*flipt.FlagList, error) {\n    // Inline comments explain complex logic\n    // Check for X-Environment header for backward compatibility\n    environmentKey := r.EnvironmentKey\n    if headerEnv, ok := common.FliptEnvironmentFromContext(ctx); ok && headerEnv != \"\" {\n        environmentKey = headerEnv\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Project Organization\n\n- Use `internal/` for private packages that shouldn't be imported externally\n- Organize by domain (`server/`, `storage/`, `config/`, `analytics/`)\n- Keep interfaces in domain root, implementations in subdirectories\n- Co-locate tests with implementation (`*_test.go`)\n- Use `testdata/` directories for test fixtures\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (Go)\n\n**Always run these commands when adding or editing Go code:**\n\n```bash\n# Format Go code\nmage go:fmt\n\n# Lint Go code\nmage go:lint\n\n# Run modernize to update code to 1.24+ style\nmage go:modernize\n```\n\n### UI/React/TypeScript Code Style\n\n#### File Naming and Organization\n\n- **Components**: Use PascalCase for `.tsx` files (`FlagForm.tsx`, `FlagTable.tsx`)\n- **API files**: Use camelCase with suffix (`flagsApi.ts`, `authApi.ts`)\n- **Types**: Use PascalCase for `.ts` files (`Flag.ts`, `Analytics.ts`)\n- **Utilities**: Use descriptive lowercase names (`helpers.ts`)\n\n#### Component Structure\n\n- Use functional components with hooks\n- Organize components by domain in directories\n- Keep reusable UI components in `ui/` directory\n- Co-locate component tests with implementation\n\n#### State Management\n\n- Use Redux Toolkit for application state\n- Create API slices for domain-specific data (`flagsApi.ts`)\n- Use TypeScript for type safety throughout\n\n#### Pre-commit Quality Checks (UI)\n\n**Always Playwright for E2E\n\n### Writing Effective Tests\n\nWhen writing tests, ensure they actually verify the functionality being tested:\n\n**❌ Bad Example - Test doesn't verify actual behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test only verifies the method runs without error, not that the logic works\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    assert.NotNil(t, result)\n}\n```\n\n**✅ Good Example - Test verifies specific behavior:**\n\n```go\n// This test verifies the actual logic and behavior\nfunc TestFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Use mock.MatchedBy to verify the correct data is passed through\n    store.On(\"Method\", mock.MatchedBy(func(ctx context.Context) bool {\n        // Verify the context contains the expected values\n        value, ok := somePackage.ValueFromContext(ctx)\n        return ok && value == expectedValue\n    }), expectedArg).Return(expectedResult, nil)\n    \n    result, err := service.DoSomething(input)\n    require.NoError(t, err)\n    \n    // Verify the actual business logic worked correctly\n    assert.Equal(t, expectedOutput, result.ImportantField)\n    store.AssertExpectations(t) // Ensures mocks were called as expected\n}\n```\n\n**Key Testing Principles:**\n\n- **Verify behavior, not just success**: Don't just check that methods return without error\n- **Test the logic**: Use `mock.MatchedBy` to verify correct data flows through the system\n- **Test edge cases**: Include tests for when conditions are met vs. not met\n- **Use meaningful assertions**: Assert on the specific values that matter to the business logic\n- **Mock verification**: Use `mock.AssertExpectations(t)` to ensure mocks were called with expected parameters\n\n### Integration Tests\n\nIntegration tests are defined in `build/testing/` and run as Mage targets. For details on available integration test targets, helpers, and how to add new integration tests, see the files in that directory:\n\n- `build/testing/integration.go` - Integration test Mage targets and configuration\n- `build/testing/integration/` - Individual integration test suites\n- `build/testing/helpers.go` - Shared test helpers\n- `build/testing/test.go` - Core test utilities\n\n## Git Workflow & Commits\n\n### Creating Effective Commits\n\n#### Commit Message Format\n\nFollow conventional commit format:\n\n```\ntype(scope): brief description\n\nLonger description if needed explaining the why, not the what.\n\n- List specific changes if helpful\n- Include any breaking changes\n- Reference issues (e.g., \"Fixes #123\")\n```\n\n#### Commit Types\n\n- `feat:` - New features\n- `fix:` - Bug fixes\n- `docs:` - Documentation changes\n- `style:` - Code style changes (formatting, etc.)\n- `refactor:` - Code refactoring without functional changes\n- `test:` - Adding or modifying tests\n- `chore:` - Build process or auxiliary tool changes\n\n#### Examples\n\n```bash\n# Good commit messages\ngit commit -s -m \"feat: add X-Environment header support to ListFlags endpoint\n\nThe v1 ListFlags endpoint now checks for X-Environment header \nfor backward compatibility. Similarly for a v1 (main) feature, use the `v1` label.\n\n#### Quality Checklist\n\nBefore creating a PR, ensure:\n\n- [ ] Code follows style guidelines\n- [ ] Tests are added and passing\n- [ ] Linting passes (`mage go:lint` / `mage ui:lint`)\n- [ ] Code is formatted (`mage go:fmt` / `mage ui:fmt`)\n- [ ] Commit messages are clear and descriptive\n- [ ] PR description explains the change and its purpose\n","numLines":571,"startLine":1,"totalLines":571}}}
